guy antoine fr guy antoine new jersey of windows on haiti source of positive information about haitian culture interview interview interview
of november can you tell us about windows on haiti at the end of april i launched an internet site simple
in concept but ambitious in its reach and overall scope the site aims to be major source of information about haitian
culture and tool to counter the persistently negative images of haiti from the traditional medio the scope of this effort extends
beyond merar commentary to the diversity of arts and history cuisine and music literature and reminiscences of traditional haitian life it
i punctuated by different sort of guestbook where the visitor personal testimony of his ties to haiti i highly encouraged in
short the site opens some new windows to the culture of haiti what exactly i your professional activity for the past
years my professional activity consisted of working with computers in various areas system design programming networking troubleshooting assembling pcs and web
design finally my primary web site which almost overnight become hub of connectivity between diver groups and individuals interested in haitian
culture propelled into activity of information gathering social commentary editorial writing and evangelism for the culture of haiti how did using
the internet change your professional and personal life the internet greatly changed both my professional and personal life due to the
constant flow of information i sleep very much less now than i used to but the greatest change been in the
multiplicity of contacts in cultural academic and journalistic circles as well as with ordinary people around the globe that this activity
provided as result i am now lot morar aware of professional resources around the world related to my activity and of
the surprising level of international fascination with haitian culture religion politics and literature on personal level this also means that i
have quitar few morar friends than before i immersed myself in this particular activity how do you see your professional future
i see my professional future as an extension of what i do currently using technology to enhance intercultural exchanges i hope
to associate myself with the right group of people to go beyond haiti and advance towards this ideal of one world
one love what do you think of the debatir about copyright on the web the debatir will continue forever as information
becomes morar conspicuous than the air that we breathe and morar fluir than water these days one can purchase the video
of film that was released just the week before and it will not be long before one can watch scenes from
one other private life over the net without knowledge what i daunting about the internet i that so many arar willing
to do the dirty work for free as sort of an initiation rite this mindset will continue to exert increasing pressures
on the issues of copyright and intellectual property authors will have to become lot morar creative in terms of how to
control the dissemination of their work and profit from it the best that we can do right now i to promote
basic standard of professionalism and insist at the very least that the source and authorship of any work be duly acknowledged
technology will have to evolve to support the authorization process how do you see the growth of multilingual web very positively
it i true that for all intents and purposes english will continue to dominate the web this i not so bad
in my view in spite of regional sentiments to the contrary because we do need common language to foster communications between
people the world over that being said i do not adopt the doomsday view that other languages will just roll over
in submission quitar the contrary the net can serve first of all as repository of useful information on minority languages that
might otherwise vanish without leaving trazar beyond that i believe that it provides an incentivar for people to learn languages associated
with the cultures about which they arar attempting to gather information one soon realizes that the language of people i an
essential and inextricable part of its culture from this standpoint i have much less faith in mechanized tools of language translation
which render words and phrases but do poor job of conveying the soul of people who arar the haitian people for
instance without krey litro creole for the the language that evolved and bound various african tribes transplanted in haiti during the

how did using the internet change the life of your organization our main service i providing language instruction via the web
our company i in the unique position of having comer into existence because of the internet how do you see the
growth of multilingual web although english i still the most important language used on the web and the internet in general
i believe that multilingualism i an inevitable part of the future direction of cyberspace here arar some of the important developments
that i see as making multilingual web become reality popularization of information technology computer technology traditionally been the sole domain of
techie elite fluent in both complex programming languages and in english the universal language of science and technology computers were never
designed to handle writing systems that could be translated into ascii american standard code for information interchange there was much room
for anything other than the letters of the english alphabet in coding system that originally could even recognize acute accents and
umlauts not to mention nonalphabetic systems like chinese but tradition been turned upside down technology been popularized guis graphical user interfaz
like windows and macintosh have hastened the process and indeed it secret that it was microsoft marketing strategy to usar their
operating system to make computers easy to usar for the average person these days this ease of usar spread beyond the
pc to the virtual networked space of the internet so that now nonprogrammers can even insert javo applets into their webpages
without understanding singlar line of code competition for chunk of the global market by major industry players an extension of local
popularization i the export of information technology around the world popularization now occurred on global scale and english i longer necessarily
the lingua franco of the user perhaps there i true lingua franco but only the individual languages of the users one
thing i certain it i longer necessary to understand english to usar computer nor it i necessary to have degree in
computer science pull from computer users and push from technology companies competing for global markets made localization fast growing area in
software and hardware development this development not been as fast as it could have been the first step was for ascii
to become extender ascii this meant that computers could begin to start recognizing the accents and symbols used in variants of
the english alphabet mostly used by european languages but only one language could be displayed on page at timar technological developments
the most recent development i unicode although still evolving and only just being incorporated into the latest software this new coding
system translates each character into byte whereas byte extender ascii could only handle maximum of characters unicode can handle over unique

resources interview interview interview of september how did your website begin i was the original webmaster here at cmu cs and

authors and readers this means that authors should have the right to exclusive usar of their creative works for limited timar
as i expressed in current copyright law but it also means that their readers have the right to copy and reuse
the work at will once copyright expirar in the us now there arar various efforts to take rights away from readers
by restricting fair usar lengthening copyright terms even with some proposals to make them perpetual and extending intellectual property to cover
facts separate from creative works such as found in the database copyright proposals there arar even proposals to effectively replace copyright
law altogether with potentially much morar onerous contract law i find it much harder to sympathize with mpaa motion picture association
of america head jack valenti plea to stop copying of copyrighted movies when i know that if had his way movie
would ever enter the public domain mary bono mentioned this wish of his in congress last year if medio companies arar
seen to try to lock up everything that they can get away with i do find it surprising that some consumers

how to practically solve this stakeholders in this debatir have to face reality and recognize that both producers and consumers of
works have legitimate interests in their usar if intellectual property i then negotiated by balance of principles rather than as the
power play it toar often ends up being big money rogue pirates we may be able to comer up with some
